Reliance on agricultural exports makes Cameroon vulnerable to shifts in their prices.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg/220px-Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg/330px-Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg/440px-Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="610" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> herder drives his cattle in northern Cameroon.</div></div></div>\n<p>Livestock are raised throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Fishing employs 5,000 people and provides over 100,000 tons of seafood each year.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-awf_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">Bushmeat</a>, long a staple food for rural Cameroonians, is today a delicacy in the country\'s urban centres. The commercial bushmeat trade has now surpassed deforestation as the main threat to wildlife in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The southern rainforest has vast timber reserves, estimated to cover 37% of Cameroon\'s total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-awf_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> However, large areas of the forest are difficult to reach. Logging, largely handled by foreign-owned firms,<sup id="cite_ref-awf_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> provides the government US$60&#160;million a year in taxes (as of  1998<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>), and laws mandate the safe and sustainable exploitation of timber. Nevertheless, in practice, the industry is one of the least regulated in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Factory-based industry accounted for an estimated 29.7% of GDP in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> More than 75% of Cameroon\'s industrial strength is located in <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bonab%C3%A9ri" title="Bonab\xc3\xa9ri">Bonab\xc3\xa9ri</a>. Cameroon possesses substantial mineral resources, but these are not extensively mined (see <i><a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining in Cameroon">Mining in Cameroon</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-State_Dept_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Petroleum exploitation has fallen since 1986, but this is still a substantial sector such that dips in prices have a strong effect on the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Rapids and waterfalls obstruct the southern rivers, but these sites offer opportunities for hydroelectric development and supply most of Cameroon\'s energy. The Sanaga River powers the largest hydroelectric station, located at Ed\xc3\xa9a. The rest of Cameroon\'s energy comes from oil-powered thermal engines. Much of the country remains without reliable power supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cameroon" title="Transport in Cameroon">Transport in Cameroon</a> is often difficult. Except for the several relatively good <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll roads</a> which connect major cities (all of them one-lane) roads are poorly maintained and subject to inclement weather, since only 10% of the roadways are tarred.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Roadblocks often serve little other purpose than to allow police and gendarmes to collect bribes from travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Road banditry has long hampered transport along the eastern and western borders, and since 2005, the problem has intensified in the east as the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> has further destabilised.<sup id="cite_ref-Musa_Gunmen_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Gunmen-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Intercity_bus_service" title="Intercity bus service">Intercity bus services</a> run by multiple private companies connect all major cities. They are the most popular means of transportation followed by the rail service <i><a href="/wiki/Camrail" title="Camrail">Camrail</a></i>. Rail service runs from <a href="/wiki/Kumba" title="Kumba">Kumba</a> in the west to <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9labo" title="B\xc3\xa9labo">B\xc3\xa9labo</a> in the east and north to <a href="/wiki/Ngaound%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Ngaound\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9">Ngaound\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> International airports are located in <a href="/wiki/Douala_International_Airport" title="Douala International Airport">Douala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9_Nsimalen_International_Airport" title="Yaound\xc3\xa9 Nsimalen International Airport">Yaound\xc3\xa9</a>, with a third under construction in <a href="/wiki/Maroua" title="Maroua">Maroua</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Douala is the country\'s principal seaport.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In the north, the B\xc3\xa9nou\xc3\xa9 River is seasonally navigable from Garoua across into Nigeria.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although press freedoms have improved since the first decade of the 21st century, the press is corrupt and beholden to special interests and political groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Reporters_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reporters-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Newspapers routinely self-censor to avoid government reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The major radio and television stations are state-run and other <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications in Cameroon">communications</a>, such as land-based telephones and telegraphs, are largely under government control.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> However, cell phone networks and Internet providers have increased dramatically since the first decade of the 21st century<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and are largely unregulated.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Armed_Forces" title="Cameroonian Armed Forces">Cameroonian Armed Forces</a></div>\n<p>The Cameroon Armed Forces, (French: <i>Forces arm\xc3\xa9es camerounaises</i>, FAC) as of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, consists of the country\'s army (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i>Arm\xc3\xa9e de Terre</i>), the country\'s navy (French: <i>Marine Nationale de la R\xc3\xa9publique</i> (MNR), includes naval infantry), the Cameroonian Air Force (French: <i>Arm\xc3\xa9e de l\'Air du Cameroun</i>, AAC), Fire Fighter Corps, Rapid Intervention Brigade and the <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Males and females that are 18 years of age up to 23 years of age and have graduated high school are eligible for military service. Those that do so are obliged 4 years of service. There is no conscription in Cameroon, but the government makes periodic calls for volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cameroon" title="Demographics of Cameroon">Demographics of Cameroon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg/440px-YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg" width="440" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a3/YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg 1.5x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaound\xc3\xa9">Yaound\xc3\xa9</a> panoramic view.</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Cameroon<sup id="cite_ref-IEApop2011_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEApop2011-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1971</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">7.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1990</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">12.2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2009</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">19.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">23.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:left;"><small>Source: OECD/World Bank</small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The population total in Cameroon was 23,439,189 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The life expectancy is 56&#160;years (55.9&#160;years for males and 58.6&#160;years for females).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the latest census, Cameroon still has slightly more women (50.6%) than men (49.4%). Nearly 60% of the population is under age 25. People over 65 years of age account for only 3.2% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cameroon\'s population is almost evenly divided between urban and rural dwellers.<sup id="cite_ref-West_3_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_3-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Population density is highest in the large urban centres, the western highlands, and the northeastern plain.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Douala, Yaound\xc3\xa9, and <a href="/wiki/Garoua" title="Garoua">Garoua</a> are the largest cities. In contrast, the Adamawa Plateau, southeastern B\xc3\xa9nou\xc3\xa9 depression, and most of the South Cameroon Plateau are sparsely populated.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 4.8 in 2013 with a population growth rate of 2.56%.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>People from the overpopulated western highlands and the underdeveloped north are moving to the coastal plantation zone and urban centres for employment.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Smaller movements are occurring as workers seek employment in lumber mills and plantations in the south and east.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Although the national sex ratio is relatively even, these out-migrants are primarily males, which leads to unbalanced ratios in some regions.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maison_obus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/300px-Maison_obus.jpg" width="300" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/450px-Maison_obus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/600px-Maison_obus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1060" data-file-height="688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maison_obus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The homes of the <a href="/wiki/Musgum_dwelling_units" class="mw-redirect" title="Musgum dwelling units">Musgum</a>, in the Far North Region, are made of earth and grass.</div></div></div>\n<p>Both <a href="/wiki/Monogamy" title="Monogamy">monogamous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamous</a> marriage are practised, and the average Cameroonian family is large and extended.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In the north, women tend to the home, and men herd cattle or work as farmers. In the south, women grow the family\'s food, and men provide meat and grow cash crops. Like most societies, Cameroonian society is male-dominated, and violence and discrimination against women is common.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Estimates identify anywhere from 230 to 282 different folks and linguistic groups in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The Adamawa Plateau broadly bisects these into northern and southern divisions. The northern peoples are Sudanese groups, who live in the central highlands and the northern lowlands, and the Fulani, who are spread throughout northern Cameroon. A small number of <a href="/wiki/Baggara" title="Baggara">Shuwa</a> Arabs live near Lake Chad. Southern Cameroon is inhabited by speakers of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-Bantu" title="Semi-Bantu">Semi-Bantu</a> languages. Bantu-speaking groups inhabit the coastal and equatorial zones, while speakers of Semi-Bantu languages live in the Western grassfields. Some 5,000 Gyele and Baka <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmy peoples</a> roam the southeastern and coastal rainforests or live in small, roadside settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Nigerians make up the largest group of foreign nationals.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="float: left;height:2.6em;"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">6</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Maroua" title="Maroua">Maroua</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">9</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Nkongsamba" title="Nkongsamba">Nkongsamba</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Southwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Southwest Region (Cameroon)">Southwest</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">90,090\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugees">Refugees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Refugees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Refugees_in_Cameroon" title="Refugees in Cameroon">Refugees in Cameroon</a></div>\n<p>In 2007, Cameroon hosted a total population of refugees and asylum seekers of approximately 97,400. Of these, 49,300 were from the Central African Republic (many driven west by war),<sup id="cite_ref-RCross_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCross-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> 41,600 from <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, and 2,900 from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Kidnappings of Cameroonian citizens by Central African bandits have increased since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Musa_Gunmen_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Gunmen-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the first months of 2014, thousands of refugees fleeing the violence in the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> arrived in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 June 2014, AlertNet reported:\n</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>Almost 90,000 people have fled to neighbouring Cameroon since December and up to 2,000 a week, mostly women and children, are still crossing the border, the United Nations said.\n</p><p>"Women and children are arriving in Cameroon in a shocking state, after weeks, sometimes months, on the road, foraging for food," said Ertharin Cousin, executive director of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (WFP).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Cameroon" title="Languages of Cameroon">Languages of Cameroon</a></div>\n<p>Both English and French are official languages, although French is by far the most understood language (more than 80%).<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> German, the language of the original colonisers, has long since been displaced by French and English. <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Pidgin_English" title="Cameroonian Pidgin English">Cameroonian Pidgin English</a> is the lingua franca in the formerly British-administered territories.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> A mixture of English, French, and Pidgin called <a href="/wiki/Frananglais" class="mw-redirect" title="Frananglais">Frananglais</a> has been gaining popularity in urban centres since the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Niba_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Niba-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The government encourages bilingualism in English and French, and as such, official government documents, new legislation, ballots, among others, are written and provided in both languages. As part of the initiative to encourage bilingualism in Cameroon, six of the eight universities in the country are entirely bilingual.\n</p><p>In addition to the colonial languages, there are approximately 250 other languages spoken by nearly 20 million Cameroonians.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> It is because of this that Cameroon is considered one of the most linguistically diverse countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017 there were language protests by the anglophone population against perceived oppression by the francophone. The military was deployed against the protesters and people have been killed, hundreds imprisoned and thousands fled the country.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">Religion in Cameroon</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5"><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">Religion in Cameroon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-pew_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">religion</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Cameroon">Catholic</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:yellow; width:40%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">40%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:blue; width:30%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">30%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Cameroon" title="Islam in Cameroon">Muslim</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:green; width:18%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">18%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">None</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:black; width:6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">Folk</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:red; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">Other</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:gray; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Cameroon has a high level of <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">religious freedom</a> and diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The predominant faith is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, practised by about two-thirds of the population, while <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is a significant minority faith, adhered to by about one-fifth. In addition, traditional faiths are practised by many. Muslims are most concentrated in the north, while Christians are concentrated primarily in the southern and western regions, but practitioners of both faiths can be found throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Large cities have significant populations of both groups.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Muslims in Cameroon are divided into <a href="/wiki/Sufis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufis">Sufis</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Salafi" class="mw-redirect" title="Salafi">Salafis</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shias</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>People from the North-West and South-West provinces, which used to be a part of <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">British Cameroons</a>, have the highest proportion of Protestants. The French-speaking regions of the southern and western regions are largely Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Southern ethnic groups predominantly follow Christian or traditional African <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animist</a> beliefs, or a <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> combination of the two. People widely believe in witchcraft, and the government outlaws such practices.<sup id="cite_ref-Geschiere_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geschiere-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Suspected witches are often subject to mob violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The Islamist jihadist group Ansar al Islam has been reported as operating in North Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the northern regions, the locally dominant Fulani ethnic group is mostly Muslim, but the overall population is fairly evenly divided among Muslims, Christians, and followers of indigenous religious beliefs (called <i><a href="/wiki/Kirdi" title="Kirdi">Kirdi</a></i> ("pagan") by the Fulani).<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bamum_people" title="Bamum people">Bamum</a> ethnic group of the West Region is largely Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Native traditional religions are practised in rural areas throughout the country but rarely are practised publicly in cities, in part because many indigenous religious groups are intrinsically local in character.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Norwegian Missionary Society first established a mission in Cameroon in the early 1920s. Many of the churches still stands. At the time there were few Christians but now there are many. In cooperation with the local Evangelical Lutheran Church of Cameroon EELC and the American ELCA the NMS built several hospitals among these the Protestant Hospital of Ngaound\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9, high schools and several other institutions. Ngaound\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9 once held one of the largest Norwegian contingencies of any place in the world, with over 100 Norwegians living there in the 1980s. Some of the families have been there in several generations among these Kaldhol, Bjaanes, Stavenjord and Dankel. The neighbourhood was even dubbed "Norv\xc3\xa8ge" ("Norway" in French).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cameroon" title="Culture of Cameroon">Culture of Cameroon</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Cameroon" title="Media of Cameroon">Media of Cameroon</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cameroon" title="Music of Cameroon">Music of Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Cameroon" title="Public holidays in Cameroon">Public holidays in Cameroon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg/220px-Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="313" data-file-height="336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dancers greet visitors to the East Region.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cameroon" title="Music of Cameroon">Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Cameroon" title="Dance in Cameroon">dance</a> are an integral part of Cameroonian ceremonies, festivals, social gatherings, and storytelling.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-West_18_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Traditional dances are highly choreographed and separate men and women or forbid participation by one sex altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The goals of dances range from pure entertainment to religious devotion.<sup id="cite_ref-West_18_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally, music is transmitted orally. In a typical performance, a chorus of singers echoes a soloist.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_189_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_189-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Musical accompaniment may be as simple as clapping hands and stomping feet,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> but traditional instruments include bells worn by dancers, clappers, drums and <a href="/wiki/Talking_drum" title="Talking drum">talking drums</a>, flutes, horns, rattles, scrapers, stringed instruments, whistles, and xylophones; the exact combination varies with ethnic group and region. Some performers sing complete songs by themselves, accompanied by a harplike instrument.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_189_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_189-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Popular music styles include <a href="/wiki/Ambasse_bey" title="Ambasse bey">ambasse bey</a> of the coast, <a href="/wiki/Assiko" title="Assiko">assiko</a> of the Bassa, <a href="/wiki/Mangambeu" title="Mangambeu">mangambeu</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bamileke" class="mw-redirect" title="Bamileke">Bangangte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tsamassi" title="Tsamassi">tsamassi</a> of the Bamileke.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nigeria" title="Music of Nigeria">Nigerian music</a> has influenced Anglophone Cameroonian performers, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Nico_Mbarga" title="Prince Nico Mbarga">Prince Nico Mbarga</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">highlife</a> hit "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Mother" title="Sweet Mother">Sweet Mother</a>" is the top-selling African record in history.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The two most popular styles of music are <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bikutsi" title="Bikutsi">bikutsi</a>. Makossa developed in Douala and mixes folk music, highlife, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">Congo music</a>. Performers such as <a href="/wiki/Manu_Dibango" title="Manu Dibango">Manu Dibango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bebey" title="Francis Bebey">Francis Bebey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moni_Bil%C3%A9" title="Moni Bil\xc3\xa9">Moni Bil\xc3\xa9</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petit-Pays" title="Petit-Pays">Petit-Pays</a> popularised the style worldwide in the 1970s and 1980s. Bikutsi originated as war music among the Ewondo. Artists such as <a href="/wiki/Anne-Marie_Nzi%C3%A9" title="Anne-Marie Nzi\xc3\xa9">Anne-Marie Nzi\xc3\xa9</a> developed it into a popular dance music beginning in the 1940s, and performers such as <a href="/wiki/Mama_Ohandja" title="Mama Ohandja">Mama Ohandja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_T%C3%AAtes_Brul%C3%A9es" title="Les T\xc3\xaates Brul\xc3\xa9es">Les T\xc3\xaates Brul\xc3\xa9es</a> popularised it internationally during the 1960s, 1970s, and 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nkolo_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nkolo-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_cuisine" title="Cameroonian cuisine">Cameroonian cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/220px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/330px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/440px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1485" data-file-height="1173" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A woman weaves a basket near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ossa" title="Lake Ossa">Lake Ossa</a>, Littoral Region. Cameroonians practise such handicrafts throughout the country.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Cameroon">Cuisine</a> varies by region, but a large, one-course, evening meal is common throughout the country. A typical dish is based on cocoyams, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> (manioc), <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, often pounded into dough-like <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>. This is served with a sauce, soup, or stew made from greens, <a href="/wiki/Groundnut" title="Groundnut">groundnuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>, or other ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Meat and fish are popular but expensive additions, with chicken often reserved for special occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_121-2_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_121-2-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Dishes are often quite hot, spiced with salt, red pepper sauce, and <a href="/wiki/Maggi" title="Maggi">Maggi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cutlery is common, but food is traditionally manipulated with the right hand. Breakfast consists of leftovers of bread and fruit with <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>. Generally breakfast is made from wheat flour in various different foods such as puff-puff (doughnuts), accra banana made from <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a> and flour, bean cakes and many more. Snacks are popular, especially in larger towns where they may be bought from <a href="/wiki/Street_vendor" class="mw-redirect" title="Street vendor">street vendors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Water, <a href="/wiki/Palm_wine" title="Palm wine">palm wine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Millet_beer" title="Millet beer">millet beer</a> are the traditional mealtime drinks, although beer, soda, and wine have gained popularity. 33 Export beer is the official drink of the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national soccer team</a> and one of the most popular brands, joining Castel, <a href="/wiki/Amstel_Brewery" title="Amstel Brewery">Amstel Brewery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinness_Foreign_Extra_Stout" title="Guinness Foreign Extra Stout">Guinness</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_arts_and_crafts">Local arts and crafts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Local arts and crafts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Traditional arts and crafts are practiced throughout the country for commercial, decorative, and religious purposes. Woodcarvings and sculptures are especially common.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The high-quality clay of the western highlands is suitable for pottery and ceramics.<sup id="cite_ref-West_18_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Other crafts include <a href="/wiki/Basket_weaving" title="Basket weaving">basket weaving</a>, beadworking, brass and bronze working, calabash carving and painting, embroidery, and leather working. Traditional housing styles make use of locally available materials and vary from temporary wood-and-leaf shelters of nomadic <a href="/wiki/Wodaabe" title="Wodaabe">Mbororo</a> to the rectangular mud-and-thatch homes of southern peoples. Dwellings made from materials such as cement and tin are increasingly common.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">Contemporary art</a> is mainly promoted by independent cultural organizations (<a href="/wiki/Doual%27art" title="Doual&#39;art">Doual\'art</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Africr%C3%A9a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Africr\xc3\xa9a (page does not exist)">Africr\xc3\xa9a</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Artist-run_initiative" title="Artist-run initiative">artist-run initiatives</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Art_Wash&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Art Wash (page does not exist)">Art Wash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atelier_Viking" title="Atelier Viking">Atelier Viking</a>, <a href="/wiki/ArtBakery" title="ArtBakery">ArtBakery</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Cameroon" title="Literature of Cameroon">Literature of Cameroon</a></div>\n<p>Cameroonian literature has concentrated on both European and African themes. Colonial-era writers such as <a href="/wiki/Louis-Marie_Pouka" title="Louis-Marie Pouka">Louis-Marie Pouka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sankie_Maimo" title="Sankie Maimo">Sankie Maimo</a> were educated by European missionary societies and advocated <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">assimilation</a> into European culture as the means to bring Cameroon into the modern world.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, writers such as <a href="/wiki/Mongo_Beti" title="Mongo Beti">Mongo Beti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Oyono" title="Ferdinand Oyono">Ferdinand Oyono</a> analysed and criticised colonialism and rejected assimilation.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Volet_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volet-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films_and_Literatures">Films and Literatures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Films and Literatures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Cameroon" title="Cinema of Cameroon">Cinema of Cameroon</a></div>\n<p>Shortly after independence, filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Ngassa" title="Jean-Paul Ngassa">Jean-Paul Ngassa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Sita-Bella" title="Th\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa8se Sita-Bella">Th\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa8se Sita-Bella</a> explored similar themes.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> In the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Mongo_Beti" title="Mongo Beti">Mongo Beti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_L%C3%A9opold_Oyono" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand L\xc3\xa9opold Oyono">Ferdinand L\xc3\xa9opold Oyono</a> and other writers explored post-colonialism, problems of African development, and the recovery of African identity.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, in the mid-1970s, filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Dikongu%C3%A9_Pipa" title="Jean-Pierre Dikongu\xc3\xa9 Pipa">Jean-Pierre Dikongu\xc3\xa9 Pipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kamwa" title="Daniel Kamwa">Daniel Kamwa</a> dealt with the conflicts between traditional and post-colonial society. Literature and films during the next two decades concentrated more on wholly Cameroonian themes.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Cameroon" title="Sport in Cameroon">Sport in Cameroon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/300px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" width="300" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/450px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/600px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="731" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> faces <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> at <a href="/wiki/Zentralstadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Zentralstadion">Zentralstadion</a> in Leipzig, 17 November 2004.</div></div></div>\n<p>National policy strongly advocates sport in all forms. Traditional sports include canoe racing and wrestling, and several hundred runners participate in the 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon_Race_of_Hope" title="Mount Cameroon Race of Hope">Mount Cameroon Race of Hope</a> each year.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Cameroon is one of the few tropical countries to have <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Cameroon at the 2002 Winter Olympics">competed</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a>.\n</p><p>Sport in Cameroon is dominated by football. Amateur football clubs abound, organised along ethnic lines or under corporate sponsors. The <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national team</a> has been one of the most successful in Africa since its strong showing in the <a href="/wiki/1982_Football_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1982 Football World Cup">1982</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cups</a>. Cameroon has won five <a href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="African Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> titles and the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2000 Summer Olympics \xe2\x80\x93 Men&#39;s tournament">2000 Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cameroon was the host country of the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Women_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Women Cup of Nations">Women Africa Cup of Nations</a> in November\xe2\x80\x93December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Cameroon women&#39;s national football team">women\'s football team</a> is known as the "Indomitable Lionesses." \n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Rights">Human Rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Human Rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Office of the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights">United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights</a> reports that Cameroon Government forces are responsible for killings, the excessive use of force, burning down of houses, arbitrary detentions and torture. UN figures indicate that more than 21,000 people have fled to neighboring countries, while 160,000 have been internally displaced by the violence, many reportedly hiding in forests.\nOn 25 July 2018,  UN High Commissioner for Human Rights <a href="/wiki/Zeid_Raad_Al_Hussein" title="Zeid Raad Al Hussein">Zeid Ra\xe2\x80\x99ad Al Hussein</a> expressed deep concern about reports of violations and abuses in the English-speaking Northwest and Southwest regions of Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" of Cameroon">Outline of Cameroon</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a CIA<span class="reference-accessdate">.
